Coincidentally, the county government held a county administration meeting on the 2nd, and it was decided that the funds would be temporarily advanced by the property management office to facilitate the reward claim.

Changshu

Adopted Son Commits Suicide by Drinking Alkali Water: Xu Zu'en, who resided in the Hedong Street of the city and worked as a silversmith, was adopted by the Zhang family of Hupu when his father, Xu Huiqing, was infertile. After growing up, he learned his father's trade. Initially, he was quite happy. However, Xu's wife, Zhang, later gave birth to a son and a daughter and began to mistreat Zu'en. At the age of twenty-five, he was still unmarried. Last June, Zu'en's adoptive father passed away, and Lei's mistreatment intensified, often accompanied by scolding. Yesterday (1st), Zu'en ordered his apprentice to boil silver bars. For unknown reasons, an argument arose. Afterwards, he secretly drank a cup of alkali water. By the time his family noticed and called for a doctor, all attempts to revive him were unsuccessful. He died in the afternoon after drinking the water at 9 am.

Robbery Occurs in the Suburbs: Not far from the two li outside Hanbei Gate in the city, Wen Lin, who worked at the cotton mill outside Dongmen, built several houses at the Xingfu ancient temple, calling it the Pingyang Villa. He had a wife and a son, who studied in the city. Only his wife and servants lived at home. Last month, after the factory closed its books, Wang returned home to rest. However, at 1 am one morning, more than ten bandits suddenly arrived, broke down the door, and entered. Everyone in the house was sound asleep. Xue Xiaoliu, the male servant in the gatehouse, heard a loud noise outside, knew something was wrong, and hurriedly tried to open the gate. However, the gate had already been locked by the bandits. The bandits then rushed into Wang's bedroom, simultaneously setting off firecrackers to simulate gunshots. The bandits ransacked the house, overturning boxes and cabinets. They then entered Wang's mother-in-law's bedroom and searched everything. After about half an hour, they left with shouts to the east. After inspecting the losses, it was estimated that two boxes of fur clothing, including fox fur robes and squirrel fur robes, were worth approximately five hundred gold yuan. Also stolen were a gold ring, a money box, several deeds, and thirty silver yuan and thirty paper yuan, totaling about one thousand yuan.

Aside from using rental income to repay construction debts, the funds will be deposited monthly at the Xixing in the town to accrue interest. After ten years, the funds will be used to open a factory for disaster victims.

The provincial government secretly sent Fang Shan, a member of the fourth section, to Yi to cooperate with the ninth company of the stationed Buddha Security Force to send troops to suppress it. As a result, more than forty key criminals were apprehended. Except for those who surrendered and were allowed to be released on bail separately and act as informants, fifteen serious criminals were escorted to Hangzhou by company commander Cheng Qiu to be handed over to the provincial government for detention and interrogation.

County Magistrate Arrested for Embezzlement: Mao Gaokun, the magistrate of Kaihua County, has been delaying the reporting and remittance of taxes since taking office. The Civil Affairs Department ordered him to come to the province and found that he had embezzled more than 7,000 yuan of public funds. He was ordered to be detained. Yesterday, he was sent to the Hangzhou County Local Court for prosecution according to law. After the criminal court prosecutor Jiang Lichun interrogated him, Mao repeatedly requested bail. The court initially set bail at 5,000 yuan in cash. As of yet, no one has been responsible for guaranteeing his bail, and he has been sent for further detention.

Ningbo

Robbery Cases Recorded: The home of the widowed Dong in Yuanpaixi Village, Fenghua, was suddenly invaded by more than ten bandits dressed in military uniforms and carrying firearms the day before last. Dong's twelve-year-old son was sleeping in bed. Dong got up to fight, and the bandit stabbed her in the leg, seriously injuring her. On the same night, Zhang Shaoyu's house in Xujiang'an was also robbed, resulting in a large loss. Also, five bandits suddenly came to the Tai straw hat shop in Yu Yao Lishan Town at two o'clock the night before last, robbing more than fifty silver dollars, dozens of straw hats, and other miscellaneous items.

Village Police Suddenly Assassinated: The home of Chen Zhongcheng, the village police officer of Cuichen Village, Erfang Village, in Yuyao North County, was suddenly visited by three thugs at midnight yesterday. They knocked on Chen's door, falsely claiming to have something to discuss. Chen's son, Ashui, opened the door and let them in. Chen also got up to greet them. The three thugs immediately took out a pistol and shot Chen. He was hit by the bullet and died instantly. Fortunately, Ashui immediately hid and was not harmed. It is unknown whether Chen's assassination was due to him leading the police to crack down on gambling, angering the gamblers.

Temple Keeper Steals Gold Buddha to Make a Fortune: Xu Ahe, a resident of Sitangtou, Yao North, was extremely poor. He ordered his wife to be a temple keeper in a temple in Lihe. Because there was a gold Buddha statue weighing eighteen pounds in her brother's temple, she stole it and took it home. Although the temple negotiated with Xu after losing the gold Buddha, Xu did not admit it. The temple monk could do nothing. After Xu obtained the gold Buddha, he treasured it at home for four years. Now that the price of gold has risen sharply, he sold it to a Shanghai bank and got 28,800 yuan.

Jiaxing

Provincial Order Exempts Compensation for Pledged Items After Robbery of Two Pawnshops: Jiaxing's Xinhe Town's Quanxie Xing and Tongyuan pawnshops were looted by bandits. The county sent Zheng Gaixiong to investigate and clarify the situation and reported to the province for approval. The province has now issued instructions to the county that the two pawnshops are exempt from compensation for all pledged items that were looted, citing previous cases. The two pawnshops are still ordered to continue operating to maintain the market and benefit the poor. The price obtained from the sale of scattered clothing in the looted and incomplete shops is also allowed to be allocated to local public welfare to simplify matters. After receiving the order, the county government has ordered the two pawnshops to comply and has copied and announced the looted shop numbers to inform all pledgers.

Apprehension of a Large Number of Bandits: Zhao Ziqing, the captain of the detective team of the Jiaxing County Public Security Bureau, and detective Huang Baojin arrested a bandit named Gao Zixiang at the Tongji Inn on Dong Dajie the day before yesterday. After interrogation, they arrested Zhang A'er, Chen Lianzhong, Wang A'da, Lao Lin, and several suspects at their addresses. The suspects confessed to the robberies at Dumen Jiuli and other places. The investigation of the remaining members of the gang is still underway.

Bengbu

The Huai River Small Steamer is Robbed Again: Banditry is rampant on the Huai River in northern Anhui. Robbing passing steamers has become commonplace. Recently, the Yu Hua small steamer of the Bengzheng class was robbed in Luoge Street. The steamer travels between Bengbu and Zhengyang. When it was anchored at Zhengyang on the day before last, six bandits wearing concealed pistols pretended to be passengers, bought tickets, and boarded the steamer, blending in with the passengers. When the steamer was towing the Dehuai steamer and two damaged sailboats downstream, the robbers suddenly appeared at the old dock in Luoge Street, Huaiyuan County, on the morning of the 27th. They claimed to be checking for contraband. Two robbers broke into the engine room and ordered the engine to be stopped. The remaining robbers searched the passenger cabins in turn, looting the entire steamer, with a total loss of four to five thousand yuan. Among them, three female students had their leather jackets stripped off. After the robbery, the robbers went ashore and left. The steamer arrived in Bengbu that night and reported it to the Water Public Security Bureau for investigation.

(A) Yanchang Petroleum Factory: The current wells that produce the most crude oil in the factory are the old well No. 1 and the new well No. 1. The total output of the two wells is 1,000 jin of crude oil per day. To expand the output, more wells must be drilled. The factory buildings can still be used. However, all the tools are old items that have been used for many years, which are not only clumsy but also extremely dangerous. It is planned to repair the machinery extensively first and purchase various parts, which will cost more than 8,000 yuan. The coal used by the factory comes from Shima, which is 60 li southwest of the factory. The road is rugged, and camels and mules are used to transport the coal. The factory's coal consumption is about 2,000 jin per day normally. If new wells are drilled, 6,000 jin or more will be required. It is planned to turn the mountain road from the factory to Shima into a car road so that large trucks can be used to transport coal, which saves time and expense. The planned cost is more than 3,000 yuan. Both matters are planned to be handled within this year. The factory is still continuing to drill. After the fourth oil well is completed, it will continue to drill. (To be continued)

Education News

Minister of Education Gao Lu Will Return to China

Paris, March 3rd, Reuters: French Minister of Education Rosden hosted a luncheon today to entertain the Chinese Envoy to France, Mr. Gao. Mr. Gao will soon return to China to take up the post of Minister of Education. Mr. Rosden delivered a speech praising Mr. Gao's work in Paris and the contribution of Chinese culture to the West. The Ministry of Education Orders All Provinces and Cities to Report on Social Education Matters:

Yesterday, the Ministry of Education sent a notice to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities to report social education matters to the ministry within one month of receiving the notice for evaluation purposes. The notice stated: "The social education situation in all provinces and cities should be reported periodically for verification. On December 11, 1918, the Ministry issued Instruction No. 1910, listing in detail the matters to be reported and the deadlines for each. Since the implementation of this instruction, many education departments and bureaus in various provinces and cities have failed to comply on time. Therefore, the Ministry has no way of understanding the social education situation in the provinces and cities. How can we evaluate and promote progress? We will re-issue the brief list of the social education matters to be reported and the deadlines specified in Instruction No. 1910 of the Ministry of Education, as listed above. Provinces and cities that have not yet submitted reports must make up for them immediately. Those who have submitted a portion of the report should check and make up for any missing portions in addition to the submitted portion. The deadline for this supplementary report is one month from the date of receipt of this document. Hereafter, all reporting deadlines should be complied with on time without further delay. This is of utmost importance. This order includes a list of reporting matters and deadlines, as follows: (1) The academic qualifications, experience, and salaries of the principals of social education institutions should be reported once every year at the end of March, June, September, and December. (2) The status of civil schools and short-term vocational training schools for farmers, workers, and merchants, and the number of new students enrolled, should be reported once every month after the start of each semester. (3) The number of graduates and their grades from civil schools and short-term vocational training schools for farmers, workers, and merchants, should be reported once every month after the end of each semester. (4) The status and number of literacy campaigns held. (5) The establishment and progress of educational halls, museums, art galleries, libraries, newspaper reading rooms, public gymnasiums, etc. (6) The discovery and preservation of antiquities, and the establishment and progress of antiquities preservation institutes. (7) Popular lectures, storytelling, the performance of drum songs, and the review of films, dramas, lyrics, and music. (8) The status of special education for the disabled and other special education situations. (9) New experiments in social education. The above four items should all be reported once every year at the end of June."

Educational Policy Guidelines for Shanxi Province

(Taiyuan Correspondence) Director Feng Sizhi of the Education Department has recently made a determination regarding education in Shanxi, resolving to exert all efforts and actively make thorough reforms. He has already drafted a document titled "Educational Policy Guidelines for Shanxi Province," which is scheduled to be presented at today's provincial government meeting for discussion, and will then serve as the standard for future policy implementation. The text is transcribed below:

Educational Policy Guidelines for Shanxi Province: These guidelines are based on the educational objectives and implementation policies passed by the National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang on March 25, 1929, the "National Education Reform Plan" resolved at the National Education Conference convened by the Ministry of Education in May 1930, and have been formulated with consideration for the unique circumstances of Shanxi society. (A) Regarding School Education: 1. Establish a School Education Design Committee to research and innovate school education programs in Shanxi. 2. Order all levels of schools throughout the province to increase the teaching of Party ideology, aiming to integrate the knowledge and morality of all students in the province under the Three Principles of the People to achieve genuine belief and diligent practice. 3. Vigorously promote women's education to ensure equal educational opportunities for both men and women, while emphasizing the cultivation of women's sound morality and preserving their unique feminine qualities to build a good family life and social life. 4. All levels of schools should uniformly emphasize physical education to cultivate a strong spirit and develop disciplined habits. 5. Kindergarten education: Each city and county throughout the province should, as a principle, establish at least one class each. Private establishments will receive appropriate subsidies from city and county governments, but must be established by Chinese individuals and employ Chinese teachers only. 6. Elementary education: (a) All existing 22,000+ primary schools in the province should focus on qualitative improvement to ensure the soundness of basic education. (b) All 400,000+ school-aged children in the province who have not yet entered school should have the opportunity to receive four years of compulsory education, during which tuition fees may be appropriately waived. (c) Encourage the establishment of two-level schools in counties and villages to extend the years of compulsory education and offer vocational supplementary courses to impart applicable knowledge of agriculture, industry, and commerce. (d) Instruct primary schools in all villages to implement moral education based on the teachings of the late Dr. Sun Yat-sen, to cultivate the national morals of "loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, harmony, and peace" in children. (e) Elementary schools at all levels should earnestly implement political training for children to cultivate students' ability to exercise the four powers (suffrage, recall, initiative, and referendum). (f) Order all counties to uniformly establish two-year or three-year short-term normal schools to cultivate excellent teachers suitable for rural schools. Within ten years, ensure that all elementary school teachers in the province are trained by normal schools. (g) Improve the service regulations for joint school principals to achieve good guidance results. (h) Eliminate illegal and unreasonable private schools. (i) Investigate the actual conditions of society as the foundation for improving rural elementary schools. 7. Secondary education: (a) Focus on qualitative improvement and quantitative increase, adopting a gradualist approach. (b) Earnestly rectify private secondary schools to achieve the unification of education. (c) Normal education must cultivate the most wholesome teachers through the most suitable scientific education and the strictest physical and mental training, and strive to develop rural normal education. 8. Higher education: In addition to striving to implement Article 4 of the implementation policy stipulated by the Third National Congress, which states, "University and vocational education must focus on practical science, enrich scientific content, cultivate specialized knowledge and skills, and truly cultivate wholesome character to serve the country and society," we plan to invite specialists to study and improve the program. 9. Vocational Education: (a) Elementary schools emphasize career education; (b) Secondary schools emphasize career guidance; (c) Vocational schools emphasize practical learning. 10. Agricultural Education: (a) Make rural schools truly become the center of rural society. (b) Compile textbooks suitable for rural elementary schools. (c) Ensure that rural education and urban education develop equally. (d) Agricultural education institutions should fully and actively implement measures to improve agricultural production methods, increase farmers' skills, improve rural organization and farmers' lives, popularize agricultural scientific knowledge, and promote farmers' production and consumption cooperation. 11. Party Boy Scout Education: (a) Continue to establish Party Boy Scout training classes to train Party Boy Scout teachers for each county. (b) All counties with Party Boy Scout teachers should strive to establish Party Boy Scout troops. (c) Instruct all normal schools to add Party Boy Scout education from the first semester to the third semester. (B) Regarding Social Education: 1. The Education Department will establish a Social Education Section to specialize in the implementation of social education. 2. Consolidate, expand, and increase the number of social education institutions run by the province. 3. Consolidate and expand social education institutions in cities and counties. 4. Stipulate that each city and county establish public libraries. 5. All city and county primary schools must establish attached adult schools to implement mass education, so that the masses throughout the province possess common knowledge of urban and rural life, skills to improve family economy, and the necessary qualifications for civic self-governance. 6. Compile literacy textbooks suitable for farmers and urban residents. 7. Organize provincial literacy movement committees to carry out literacy movements to reduce illiteracy. 8. Establish a phonetic symbols promotion committee to vigorously promote the popularization of phonetic symbols to increase the knowledge of out-of-school people. 9. Operate public entertainment facilities in cities and counties. (C) Regarding Physical Education: 1. Establish a Shanxi Physical Education Promotion Committee to study plans for the implementation of school physical education and social physical education. 2. Order each city and county to establish public sports fields to develop public physical education. 3. In addition to all levels of schools emphasizing physical education, also order all schools above the secondary level to receive appropriate military training. (D) Regarding Educational Administration: 1. Propose to revise the regulations for education bureaus in each county of Shanxi, submitting them to the provincial government to order each county to organize and implement them within a time limit, to unify educational administration and achieve the effects of educational specialization. 2. Convene regular meetings of county education administrators to discuss matters that should be promoted and reformed in education.

Regulations for Preliminary Entrance Examinations for Graduates of Unregistered Private Senior High Schools

Last summer, the Ministry of Education held preliminary entrance examinations for graduates of unregistered private senior high schools. Because this was an initiative, many people were cautious and hesitant, resulting in few applicants and a limited number of those admitted. Later, various public and private universities reported the status of new students, and it was found that some admitted graduates from unregistered schools. The Ministry of Education refuted this and canceled their admission qualifications. Requests for flexibility from provincial and municipal education departments were also not permitted. This matter is not merely a bureaucratic formality but will be strictly enforced. Therefore, many provinces and cities requested relief. Last month, the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau requested permission to hold another preliminary entrance examination for graduates of unregistered private senior high schools in July of this year, following the previous example. The Ministry of Education, in addition to instructing the bureau to approve this, also ordered all provincial and municipal education departments to uniformly hold an examination on July 1, and to develop examination regulations based on the principles of the preliminary entrance examination regulations issued by the Ministry of Education last year and submit them to the Ministry for record. The original text of the regulations is as follows: "Principles of the Preliminary Entrance Examination Regulations for Graduates of Unregistered Private Senior High Schools: (1) Establish an examination committee composed of one chairman and six to ten members. (2) The head of the provincial or municipal education administrative agency shall be the ex officio chairman. The members shall be appointed or hired by the provincial or municipal education administrative agency from among current education administrators and principals and teachers of current public or registered private high schools or higher. However, the number of administrative personnel shall not exceed one-third of the number of principals and teachers. (3) The examination subjects shall be based on the curriculum of public senior high schools or equivalent schools. (4) This examination shall be held in the location of the provincial or municipal government. (5) Those who pass the examination shall be given a certificate of admission to higher education, and those who fail shall be given a certificate of transfer to a lower grade according to their level." The aforementioned certificate of admission to higher education shall state: "(This certificate is only for admission to higher education and shall not be used for proving other qualifications)." The same shall apply to the certificate of transfer. (6) Graduates of vocational schools who have completed three years of study after graduating from junior high school shall be permitted to register for the examination.

Student Unrest at Anhui University

▲Students Attack the Chief of General Affairs

At around 12:00 PM on the day before yesterday (February 26), students such as Xie Yinrong, incited by expelled students such as Wu Zhaoshu, stormed into the dormitory of Xue Liangshu, the Chief of General Affairs of Anhui University, arbitrarily insulting and berating him, and forcing him to leave the school. Later, when Xue reached near Baihua Pavilion, five people, including Wu Zhaoshu, ambushed him there, hitting him head-on, smearing him with mud, and snatching away Xue's glasses. Fortunately, a police officer noticed this and stopped them, saving Xue from danger. After receiving this news, the school immediately convened an emergency school affairs meeting and an administrative meeting, which resolved to express condolences to Xue Liangshu in the name of the school affairs meeting, and sent representatives to visit Chairman Chen to report the incident. The Chairman was extremely angry at the outrageous academic atmosphere and immediately ordered the Public Security Bureau to arrest and investigate the previously expelled student Wu Zhaoshu and others, and ordered the school to expel the students involved in this incident, and have the Public Security Bureau send police to escort them out of the province. Now the school has complied with the order and announced the expulsion of Xie Yinrong, Li Yilei, Yao Jing, Xu Yuanyu, Hao Suzhi, Luo Guanhua, Liu Yiqun, Li Yida, Du Jizhou, Miao Haiming, Hong Gen, and eleven other students who caused the disturbance.

Local News

Director Xu of the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau Discusses the District Issues of the Municipal Education Association

The Education News Agency reported that the issue of district divisions for the Shanghai Municipal Education Association has recently drawn much attention from all sectors. A reporter from the Education News Agency visited Director Xu Peihuang yesterday. The following is a record of Mr. Xu's remarks: According to Article 6 of the Education Association Law, the districts of the education association shall be based on the existing administrative districts. According to the municipal government's administrative districts, there are seventeen districts in total: Huna, Zhabei, Yinxiang, Yangjing, Yinhang, Wusong, Jiangwan, Pengpu, Zhenru, Pusong, Fahua, Caojing, Yangsi, Tangqiao, Lixing, Gaohang, and Gaoqiao, as well as the two concessions as a special district, making a total of eighteen districts. According to the law, each municipal education association should be established according to the above-mentioned district divisions. Earlier, the bureau received an order from the Ministry of Education urging the establishment of municipal education associations in all districts before March 15, and immediately notified everyone. However, in recent days, the Municipal Party Headquarters has repeatedly sent letters stating that this division is inconvenient for guiding the municipal education association and requesting alternative arrangements. After careful consideration by the bureau, it was believed that Article 6 of the Education Association Law stipulates that the districts of the district education association may be subject to exceptions if there are special circumstances and the approval of the supervisory authority is obtained. The bureau, as the legal supervisory authority, has the power to make changes. However, this matter is of great importance and should not be decided immediately. After consultation with Central Committee member Zhu Jiahua and members of the Municipal Party Headquarters on the evening of the 2nd, it was decided to change the districts of the Shanghai Municipal Education Association to eleven districts for the sake of facilitating the guidance of the Party Headquarters, and to use the districts divided by the Party Headquarters as the districts. Because it was late, it could not be announced. The bureau will issue a notice tomorrow.

Rong Zongjing Donates the West River to Great China University

West of the new campus of Great China University on Zhongshan Road, there is a river that flows from the north of the school, through the sports field and Liva Lida Ko, directly to the Suzhou Creek. It covers an area of more than sixty acres, with deep water, wide banks, and clear water. Swimming fish and fine algae are clearly visible. Willows hang over the banks, creating interesting reflections. The scenery is excellent and unique in Shanghai. The river was originally the property of Rong Zongjing, a giant flour merchant from Wuxi, and has now been donated to Great China University by Mr. Rong. Since acquiring the river, the school has dredged it for leisure fishing, boating, and swimming. The school considers Mr. Rong's generous donation and ardent enthusiasm to be commendable, and plans to submit a request to the Ministry of Education to commend him in accordance with regulations to recognize his virtues.

Expansion Plan of Kwong Chow School

▲Funds Already Secured

The Kwong Chow School in Shanghai has been operating for many years and has achieved remarkable results. It currently has more than one thousand students, and the original school buildings are insufficient for use. It has now been decided to add new buildings near Jiangwan Road to expand the school. The planned project, including land purchase, construction, and equipment costs, requires approximately 350,000 yuan. A renowned and enthusiastic educator has been entrusted to be responsible for raising funds. Since the funds are no longer an issue, construction will begin soon. The school's expansion plan is transcribed below: (1) "Construction": Purchase 50 acres of land and construct several modern and suitable classrooms, auditoriums, libraries, dormitories, gymnasiums, dining halls, and several athletic fields, ball fields, and swimming pools. (2) "Expenses": Land purchase will cost approximately 60,000 yuan, construction will cost approximately 250,000 yuan, and equipment will cost approximately 40,000 yuan, totaling approximately 350,000 yuan. The above expenses are planned to be entirely raised through donations from fellow countrymen at home and abroad who are enthusiastic about education. Recurring expenses will be borne by the Shanghai Kwong Chow Guild Hall. (3) "Adding Senior High School": In the first year after the completion of the new school buildings, add the first grade of senior high school, add the second grade in the following year, and complete all grades of senior high school in the third year, and appropriately operate vocational, commercial, and normal school departments. (4) "Allocation of School Buildings": The old school buildings will be used exclusively for junior primary school and kindergarten. The new school buildings will be used exclusively for middle school and affiliated senior primary school. (5) "Enrollment": 200 kindergarten students, 500 junior primary school students, 500 senior primary school students, 400 junior middle school students, and 400 senior middle school students, totaling 2,000 students.

Yu Guoqi, Yu Jingyi, and Huang Weili Depart for Belgium

Yu Guoqi and Yu Jingyi, the nephews of the Dean of the College of Arts and Sciences of Fudan University, and their nephew Huang Weili, plan to study in Belgium at their own expense. They are scheduled to depart from Shanghai on the Japanese liner Fushimi Maru on March 31. All three graduated from Fudan University successively. After graduation, Yu Guoqi worked as a secretary for the Jianren Company in Shanghai, Yu Jingyi worked at the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, and Huang Weili taught in both the middle school divisions of Fudan University. They are prolific writers and have published in various newspapers and magazines. Now that the three are traveling abroad together, Yu Guoqi and Yu Jingyi plan to enter the University of Leuven in Belgium to study railway management, municipal management, and other subjects. Huang Weili plans to study engineering at the University of Ghent. In the future, when they complete their studies and return to China, they will surely benefit society greatly.

Vocational Introduction Department of the Chinese Chemical Industry Association

Since its establishment in 1922, the Chinese Chemical Industry Association has gradually developed its activities. As a result, the association has more contact with factories. To facilitate both technicians and the industry, a vocational introduction department has been established. Free Talk

World Anecdotes

— Hai Ke

▲ Italy's electric railway. Its length ranks first in Europe, totaling one hundred and seventy miles.

▲ Pela City in Portuguese West Africa. Built on sand dunes, the sand is extremely deep, and horses cannot travel. Therefore, a railway was built, with laborers hand-pushing small carts to transport passengers and goods.

▲ There is a chair in London that is three thousand years old. Recently, it was publicly auctioned. The owner and buyer are unknown.

▲ The healthy African chimpanzees in the British zoo are priced at sixty to one hundred gold pounds.

▲ Coal carts in Berlin, the capital of Germany, are specially permitted by local authorities to travel on sidewalks for easy unloading when delivered to homes.

▲ American railways have built glass-lined pools specifically for transporting milk between major cities.

▲ In Tiwenfu Tuopei in England, a clear spring suddenly gushes out from the seabed one hundred yards offshore. The water quality is extremely clear and completely different from seawater.

▲ Germany has invented an airplane. The engine has fifty horsepower and can carry three passengers. It can fly one hundred miles per hour and is extremely lightweight.

▲ In Tinaneke, USA, local authorities strictly monitor dance halls. Anyone who dances irregularly in the dance hall will immediately be given a small piece of paper by the inspector, which reads: "Do not sway to the side" or "Change your dancing style."

Hongwei's Sentimental Recollections of Dunan

— A Dan

Yesterday, I received a letter from Yazi, saying that our colleague Fu Dungen died of illness in Anqing. Another member of the Southern Society has passed away. The sadness upon hearing the news is indescribable. Dungen was from Liling, Hunan. His original name was Xiong Xiangxuan, later changed to Zhuan. He was skilled in poetry and classical prose. In his early years, he devoted himself to revolution and was friendly with Ning Taiyi, Chen Tuian, and others. He and the editor were responsible for compiling the "Dongting Bo Magazine." After the Pingxiang Uprising failed in the Bingding year, Ning was arrested. The Qing officials investigated him closely. He fled to the sea. In the Gui Chou year, Tang Xiangming supervised Hunan and conducted a major search for party members. Dungen's name was listed. So, he fled from Changsha to Liling, seeking refuge at people's homes, but no relatives or friends dared to take him in. He was in dire straits. A courtesan named Huang Yujiao, with a beautiful face and a generous nature, had the spirit of a chivalrous woman. Dungen, under the assumed name of Zhang Lu, followed the example of Du Mu seeking spring, accompanied by Gong Jiemi and Huang Xuyuan. He hid in Yujiao's house. Yujiao fell in love with him at first sight, but noticing his extreme destitution, she inquired about him and learned that he was a party member. She admired and loved him even more. She generously set up a quiet room for him to live in and provided everything for him. Yujiao took care of everything. Dungen was very grateful and vowed to repay her. After ten days, the investigators relaxed a bit, and he secretly fled. After the incident was resolved, he tried to find her, but she had moved with her entire family, and her whereabouts were unknown. When asked, some villagers said she had married, others said she had died. Reliable information was hard to come by. Dungen was depressed for months and wrote "Hongwei's Sentimental Recollections" to pass on her story. Many literary figures across the country composed poems for it. There are two accompanying illustrations, created by Huang Binhong and Cai Zhefu.

Dungen once taught in Wangxianzhen. The town was named after the immortal Prince Qiao. The characters of Yujiao's name, with the strokes removed, also fittingly become Wang Qiao. Thus, he realized that encounters in life have their own causes. "Hongwei's Sentimental Recollections" casually writes about kindness and resentment, hence the name "Hongwei Sheng." He also heard that there was a Wang Dungen in Shanghai, whose name was similar to his assumed name, so he wrote to Dungen to become literary friends. He then changed his name to Dunan or simply wrote Dungen.

In recent years, Dungen served as a secretary in the provincial government, a member of the provincial assembly, the magistrate of Yuanjiang County, and the director of the Zhongshan Library. Last year, Changsha suffered two robberies, and ten thousand volumes of books were turned to ashes. He fled to Hankou, covered in dust. His colleagues did not recognize him. He then recuperated at Xiaotianchi in Mount Lu. Before long, Jiujiang was in a state of emergency, so he fled to Anqing. His illness worsened. He kept it a secret and wrote calligraphy and poems for pleasure. On the eve of his death, he still wrote a couplet for Zou Qiushi, gathering lines from Ding An's poems: "Arrange to write a collection of three thousand volumes, plan to watch the mountains for fifty years."

Dungen once traveled to West Lake and visited Songzhuang, ascending Jing Su Pavilion. A gardener presented two lotus flowers and said with a smile to his companions, "I will come to this pavilion as a god one day. You two must come in time and not forget to offer flowers to me." The guest said, "If you become a god, please inform us in advance, and we two will come to accompany you." Dungen jokingly said, "It is almost what is called 'begging for a beautiful appearance and temples to sit with me, coming in another body as the Water Immortal King'." Now, Dungen's death coincides with the time when water lilies bloom. Unexpectedly, the joke of that day became a prophecy. Alas, life is like a dream. There is truly something unbearable to speak of.

Dungen's published works include "Several Volumes of Dunan's Poems," "Commentary on the Lisao," "Duan's Annotations on the Shuowen Bubu," "Liling Local Chronicle," "Introduction to National Studies," "Essentials of Philology," "Qionghu Poetry Collection," "Essentials of Journalism," "Hongwei's Sentimental Recollections," and "A Brief Account of the Liling Military Disaster," each in one volume, "Zhongshan Library Catalog" in two volumes, "National Language Textbooks" in several volumes. Works awaiting publication include "Several Volumes of Dunan's Prose," "Dunan's Poems After the Jiazi Year," "Baiyun's Poetry Talks," "Hongwei Hall," "Collection of Stone Inscriptions from the Han Dynasty," "Tired Old Man's Travel Manuscripts," "Cloud Travel Daily Records," "Rebirth Travel Manuscripts," "Rebirth Diary," "Methods of National Studies Research," and "Duan An's Random Notes," and "Literary Series."

Discovery of the Imperial Seal of the Former Qing Dynasty

— Ou Qiu

The imperial seal of the former Qing Dynasty was lost for a long time. Now it has suddenly been discovered in the hands of a Singaporean overseas Chinese named Chen Zhen. Is this not a strange tale? Examining its origins, it dates back to the Boxer Rebellion in 1900 (the 27th year of the Guangxu reign). The Eight-Nation Alliance attacked and broke through Beijing. Guangxu fled in haste, and in the rush, he did not have time to bring out the imperial seal. When the Allied forces entered the city, they carried out a large-scale search and looting. All ancient artifacts and rare treasures were taken. The imperial seal was acquired by an American sailor. At first, the sailor did not know what it was. Seeing that it was contained in a brocade box and attached with yellow silk, he knew it must be a treasure, so he hid it and took it home. Later, the sailor went to Manila to visit a friend, but he did not find him, and his funds were exhausted. He had no way to return home, so he had to pawn the imperial seal to the Chinese consulate to get money to return to his hometown. The consul thought of returning it to the royal family and carefully preserving it. Unexpectedly, he died suddenly due to illness. Recently, his family sent the seal to his relative Chen Zhen, asking him to sell it for a good price. Chen believed that the imperial seal was of great importance and could not bear to see it fall into the hands of foreigners and become a topic of gossip, so he decided to pay a huge price to properly preserve it. The seal is a five-inch square, made of jadeite jade. The green spots are bright and radiant. The handle is carved with two dragons. The engraved ancient seal script is unfortunately unidentifiable.

A Glimpse of the Antiquities Exhibition

— Xie Fei

The History and Archaeology Group of the National Central Research Institute conducted three excavations at the Yin Ruins site in Xiaotun Village, Henan, in 1928 and 1929. In 1930, they also excavated at Chengziya, Licheng, Shandong. The artifacts obtained have been successively repaired, classified, and arranged. The essence of them was selected for exhibition at the Natural History Museum on Chengxian Street in the capital from February 21st to 23rd. Lectures were also given publicly at the Zhongda University on the afternoons of the 21st and 23rd, with slides shown to make it easier for the audience to understand. As I was nearby, I had already heard about Mr. Li Ji's lecture, so I visited the next day to admire the antiquities.

▲ Ancient and Mottled The next day, Mr. Zhang Ruzhou and I received admission tickets from the general affairs office of the Central Research Institute and walked about two hundred steps north to reach the Natural History Museum. The museum usually displays a large number of bird and animal specimens. Now, two rooms upstairs are empty. Upon entering, the ticket collector gifted a copy of the "Overview of Archaeological Work and Catalog of Exhibits." Each person received one copy, which could be used to cross-reference with the exhibits. The intention was very good. We first entered the antiquities room, which was divided into two major categories: items unearthed from Xiaotun Village, Anyang, and items unearthed from Chengziya, Licheng. The former consisted of 428 items, and the latter consisted of 120 items, totaling 548 items. The Xiaotun items were from the Yin Ruins: turtle shells, animal bones, texts, stone tools, shell tools, pottery shards, bone tools, etc. The Chengziya items were single-color pottery, shell tools, and divination bones from the Stone Age in Shandong. The smaller items were all embedded in glass boxes according to their type, allowing people to observe the traces of their comparative evolution. A silver triangular stand was placed next to the boxes, with a descriptive note indicating the land location, item name, number of items, and age in detail. The larger pottery items were all glued together from their broken pieces to restore the beauty of their form. Although the number of items was not large, the arrangement was unique, allowing people to feel a sense of nostalgia for the past and the country among the scattered bones and stones. Many work photos were hung on the four walls, with scenes of frozen villages and earthen mounds, making people yearn for them.

▲ Clear and Vivid The east room was a display of Ming and Qing historical materials. The archives of the Ming and Qing dynasties had almost been scattered among the people, and later they were transferred to the Central Research Institute for sorting by the Institute of History. What is currently displayed is a portion of them. Imperial edicts and memorials are all carefully mounted and readable. The deeds of Zheng Chenggong, Mao Wenlong, and Yuan Chonghuan can be gleaned from them. The foundation of the tribute system and the memorials of vassalage can also be seen. After the Manchus succeeded the Ming Dynasty, they used the new dynasty to rule the world and suppressed and confused many facts of the former Ming Dynasty, calling them chaotic and disordered. What is desired is to organize their biographies from the piles of old paper and to guard what is missing and delve into what is confused. It is even more necessary to eagerly expect the gentlemen of the Institute to draw from this and enter deeply.

Truly, as Mr. Li Ji said, the excavation of antiquities serves two purposes: one is to determine the history of Chinese ancient Stone Age culture, and the other is to refute the European theory that the Han Chinese came from the West. Now, the excavation of antiquities is sufficient to support these two theories and to prove that ancient Chinese culture was not created by a single phenomenon but was the convergence of multiple forces, which continues to this day in a process of division and integration. The rise of learning is always based on the discovery of ancient artifacts and ancient books. Now there are more and more ancient artifacts, but fewer and fewer ancient books. In the past, the Fenyu fell and foreign words returned. Can one not sigh?

Loujiang's Fond Memories

— Zhang

My Tai is near the river and surrounded by water, residing in the lower reaches of the Lou River. The folk customs are simple and honest, and the government is simple and the laws are clear. It is known as a land of peace and happiness. Unexpectedly, in recent years, lake bandits and sea pirates have taken the opportunity to steal and commit crimes. Kidnappings have occurred one after another, and the villagers are uneasy. The local strength is empty, and there is no way to defend themselves. Although there are virtuous officials, there is no way to govern. Those who have left their posts one after another include Yuan Gong Xiluo and Tao Gong Mu, both of whom are excellent in learning and conduct and are outstanding figures of their time. Tao Gong was dismissed after only four months. Yuan Gong was in office for one year and four months, and then resigned with a request for the people because the area was not peaceful. The townspeople missed him even more. Yuan Gong was the younger brother of Mr. Guanlan and a senior revolutionary. He was humble and modest in nature, and the entire town praised him. He inspected each township every month to understand the people's hidden concerns and paid special attention to agriculture. He personally led the people in capturing locusts and treating rice borers, and he personally led his subordinates to guide the capture and eradication. He lectured to the villagers, repeating himself many times. When he went on patrol, he always wore a long blue cloth shirt and rode in a small car, with a very simple entourage. He had the style of a commoner county magistrate, and he was approachable and kind to people. He hated opium the most. He once personally arrested a smoker and put him in jail. He usually liked to chant poems and had many good ones. He was skilled in calligraphy, and he responded to all requests. On the day he left office, the viewers blocked the road, and they all sighed that the worthy magistrate could not stay long. The poems of farewell from the townspeople have many good records. Mr. Jin Yimou's poem says: "The dawn sun in the pupils of Zhao Bao Mountain, the beauty of the Shu River shows the brilliance of a strange scholar. Remember when you were chosen as a Buddha in the young age, competing to be on the dragon gate of the forehead. The chest is full of history, the brush is used to write Su and Huang characters. The flag turned the revolutionary stone city, hand holding the golden seal Mingtang servant. (The former Premier took office as temporary President, and he was the representative who awarded the seal.) The hate-filled demons have crooked noses. The round gallbladder alone supports the body, and the iron statue slays the traitors and casts the river bank. (Qi Xieyuan harmed the Su, Mr. Shou Chang proposed casting iron statues to be placed in various disaster areas) For thirty years, the heart and blood have been exhausted, and the plan has changed and the time has passed. The whistling chrysanthemum is fragrant in the evening, hoping to follow the example of the former sages and learn to be an official. Shiyuan is indeed not a hundred-mile talent, and the government urges the people and works diligently to comfort the people. Knowing that the green bamboo spring is burnt, there are many critics in the world today. Spring mother dreams of ashes, and fluttering away to return to the field. The owls roar wildly, and the phoenix is silent, the yin and yang are reversed, as if it is. Even if I am ashamed of not being Dantai, why should I interfere in public affairs. Just because the people cherish the virtuous magistrate, this intention is clear as autumn water. I sadly drink goodbye to Dongdu, and the distant fragrance of herbs sends love to the horizon. Let's look at the bamboo horse to welcome him in the coming years. The original bad 相斯 is even waiting to be restored." Yuan Gong's departure has made it clear that the annual political achievements are not there. To seek herdsmen for the people is to be trapped in the grass. Keeping the integrity of the group laughs foolishly, and the soldiers guarding the Kou have their own husbands. It is fortunate that the locusts are no longer seen, and the painful bridge is not yet fully laid. Hang your hat today and return to the past. "I can't compare with Yuanming's old house." All are historical records. Also, the Demon Buddha said, "The Demon Buddha stands side by side, and there is a Demon where there is a Buddha. If the Demon disappears, the Buddha will not be seen, and the world will be confused." A work with feelings. (Unpaid)

Travels in Southeast Asia (129)

— Ling Hua

Children in Bassein and Yangon all play the game of flying kites, often raising them on the roofs of houses to fly them. Although there is not much wind like in China, they can still fly into the clouds for several feet. I don't understand the reason. In China, I heard people say that once Qingming passes, the earth's energy no longer rises, and kites can no longer be flown. Therefore, people do it in the second month of the yin calendar. It is now the eighth or ninth month of the yin calendar here, so I don't understand why they can be flown. In Bassein, there is a small skill, which is making gas lamps that can be released into the air, which are very beautiful. The method is to use cotton paper to paste together a lamp that is five or six feet high in diameter. (Any size is fine, but larger ones are easier to lift). First, burn tung oil rope to fill it with smoke, which can be held by two people to prevent it from flying away. Once the smoke is full, light the tung oil rope at the base of the lamp and let it rise. The lamp will rise, and a string of small candle lamps can be attached below to make a tail. They come in all colors and are very beautiful in the sky. These lamps don't cost much and are easy to make. You can learn after watching it once. I often saw people flying them in Bassein. When I asked, they said they were made by the Fujianese. As the sun sets and the moon rises, they often float in the sky and are called Zhuge lamps. The Fujianese said that they are common in Fujian, but I have never seen them in Shanghai. It is possible that they are made by the Burmese, but I don't know. However, there is a danger, which is that if they fall on a thatched roof, they can easily cause a fire.

In Guangdong and Japan, I have seen the show of a beauty turning into a skeleton. It costs a dime each time to watch. The method is very simple, but very ingenious. You see a living beauty, and when a light shines on her, she suddenly gradually turns into a white skeleton, and then gradually returns to her original form and is still a beauty. I couldn't understand how it was done. People said it wasn't an X-ray mirror. When I was in Penang, Master Fakong was very talented and said he could do it, but unfortunately I didn't get to learn from him.

Some people use silver bowls to ask for money. I was surprised when I first saw it. A friend said, "We used to say that silver bowls were used to beg for food. This saying is now proven in Burma." The beggar holding a silver bowl is not a beggar, but a street leader of the neighborhood. I looked at the bowl, which was eight inches in diameter and four inches high, with glittering silver flowers. The bowl-holder stands respectfully in front of each business's door. Each business routinely contributes silver and copper coins, regardless of whether they are Burmese, Western, or Chinese. They all give alms respectfully and without stinginess. This is the method of regularly soliciting alms to support the monks.

Commercial News, Financial Gold Standard, Stable Attitude

▲ Trend Towards Peace Yesterday, March 3rd, the gold standard situation was relatively peaceful. The market turned from high to low in the morning, and then stabilized in the afternoon, eventually rising slightly. Throughout the day, it only fluctuated around seven taels. The intention of the industry was stable, but the trading situation was complex. Yuan Maoyong, Chunyuanyong, and joint hedging all bought in. Chengfengyong, Qianchangxiangyuantai, etc., all occupied the selling side. Probably because the foreign exchange was slightly stable, the listed prices were as before, and the overseas silver market reported lower, so the price opened higher. Afterwards, sellers were eager, and bills of exchange were tight, so they were flat, so the trend was small. From seven hundred and seventy-six or seven taels, it was reduced to about seventy taels. Flour Market Finally Declines

Yesterday's flour market saw a mostly stable market in the morning session. Although Yang wheat quotations were still slightly different by two, three, or four jiao, the public was quite stable due to the rainy weather, with very slight changes compared to the previous day's closing. When the afternoon session opened, the situation did not improve due to multiple long positions from outside the industry, and all months saw a pullback. Major manufacturers, with surplus Yang wheat on order, still disregarded everything and frequently engaged in frantic selling. As a result, both near and far periods fell sharply. Given the expanded amount of selling by manufacturers, and if actual sales cannot follow, optimism is not warranted. As a result, the current month was down 2.75 cents from the previous day, April was down 2.25 cents, May was down 2.5 cents, and June to August were all down 2.25 cents.

Local News

City Finance Bureau Director Reports on Financial Situation

▲ Yesterday Evening's Reception for Newspaper Reporters

▲ Announcement of Business Tax Rate Awaits

▲ This Year's Budget May Increase by One Million

City Finance Bureau Director Tang Naikang held a banquet at the Public Servants' Club at 43 Weihaiwei Road yesterday evening at 7:00 PM to entertain newspaper reporters and report on the general situation of the Finance Bureau's business. More than ten representatives from newspapers such as Shen Bao, Min Guo Ri Bao, Xin Wen Bao, Shi Bao, and Shi Shi Xin Bao attended. During the banquet, Mr. Tang rose to give a speech, saying, approximately, "Thank you all for not disdaining and gracing us with your presence. I am deeply honored. I have been in office for eight months now, and I would like to report to you on my experiences over the past half-year."

▲ Revenue and Expenditure Situation: The budgeted income for the 19th year was 6.5 million yuan, and the budgeted expenditure was 7,024,183 yuan. This included 500,000 yuan for repaying old debts, over 820,000 yuan for public welfare subsidies, 200,000 yuan for temporary expenses, and over 320,000 yuan for reserve funds allocated according to the trial budget regulations. The amount used to cover the regular needs of various agencies was 5.2 million yuan. Breaking this down by percentage, the municipal government accounted for 5.1%, the Finance Bureau 6.8%, the Public Security Bureau 27.2%, the Education Bureau 20.5%, the Land Bureau 5.3%, the Social Affairs Bureau 4.1%, the Public Works Bureau 17.0%, the Public Utilities Bureau 5.0%, the Health Bureau 4.7%, the Port Authority 2.2%, the urban area 1.1%, and various committees 1.0%. Compared to the previous year's budget, the Public Works and Education Bureaus saw the largest increases, while other bureaus experienced slight increases. The overall revenue and expenditure showed a shortfall of more than 500,000 yuan. Potential sources of revenue to offset this shortfall include the Jiangsu Provincial Government's outstanding allocation for police salaries, which, after deducting subsidies for the Shangbao counties, still leaves a balance of tens of thousands of yuan. Additionally, the recovery of wharf taxes and the abolition of the 2.5% South City property tax could generate tens of thousands of yuan in additional revenue annually. However, all of the above are draft budgets for the 19th year and have not yet been approved and implemented. Therefore, all expenditures, except for those that are necessary and have been specifically approved, follow the previous year's budget. However, a comprehensive calculation shows that the monthly expenses required are not much different from the new budget. Speaking specifically of the income and expenditure situation in the first half of the year, the net income was more than 2.89 million yuan, and the net expenditure was more than 3.42 million yuan. (This included approximately 80,000 yuan in regular expenses for the Fire Brigade, Security Corps, and Local Self-Government Training Institute, which were not included in the original budget, as well as over 600,000 yuan in various temporary expenses that were approved later.) The revenue and expenditure already showed a deficit of more than 520,000 yuan. In addition, various transactions, such as the recovery of the South City wharf, used the guarantee deposits paid by shipping companies to offset the shortfall, and the municipal treasury allocated more than 100,000 yuan, which was not included. Approximately 600,000 yuan is still owed for emergency expenses. Furthermore, the province's outstanding payments have not yet been allocated, and the recovery of wharf taxes and the abolition of the 2.5% South City property tax in the first half of the year have not been realized. Therefore, the financial situation is deeply difficult. This is the general situation. As for this year's budget, it may increase to approximately 7.5 million yuan.

▲ Organization of Finance Council: When I first took office, I realized that the Finance Bureau lacked a consultative body, which often led to misunderstandings regarding local opinions. Therefore, in September of last year, I submitted a proposal to the Municipal Government to establish a Finance Advisory Committee. Local financial and economic experts, as well as those with financial experience, were invited to serve as committee members. Regular meetings are held monthly, and any important administrative matters of the Bureau that are deemed necessary for discussion are submitted to the committee for review. Committee members can also raise opinions on financial measures at any time for discussion. By pooling wisdom and working together, progress can be made. The establishment of this committee is truly a way to make finances more transparent, and both the government and the people benefit from it. The committee members are concerned about municipal affairs and are enthusiastic about their work, which is something we deeply appreciate. In addition, the Bureau's publications have only included one type: business reports. Each year, one is published, containing the policy situation and revenue and expenditure statistics for that year, which are all past events. The publication period is too long, and citizens concerned about finances often find it difficult to understand the actual financial situation at the time. Since I took office, I have strongly advocated for financial transparency, believing that the Bureau's publications must be expanded to meet the expectations of citizens. Therefore, I have created the Shanghai Finance Quarterly. In addition to regularly publishing the city treasury's revenue and expenditure situation and financial progress, it also broadly solicits papers from domestic financial and economic experts and translates European and American financial works for research and reference. The first issue of the publication has already been printed and distributed to various sectors, and the second issue will also be published soon and sent to you for correction.

▲ Rectification of Tax Revenue: Since the Bureau abolished the contractor system for ship taxes on November 1, 1929, and took over self-management, the monthly revenue of various ship tax offices has increased. However, the process of collecting missed and supplementary taxes on ships has been extremely complex. Therefore, the ship tax regulations have been carefully revised. On the one hand, strict investigation is used to prevent evasion, and on the other hand, supplementary taxes are reduced to show consideration. Since the announcement of the revised regulations on December 1 of last year, operations have been more convenient, and shipowners have been relieved of some difficulties. In addition, Wusong sand fishing vessels, which have always been levied secondary taxes at reduced rates based on their class, have now been approved to be uniformly changed to monthly taxes, in order to avoid disputes and ensure fairness. Furthermore, the property tax in this city was reorganized in the winter of 1927, abolishing the name of general tax and uniformly changing to property tax. The tax rate was set at 10% for residential households and 14% for shops, and all districts followed it. However, in the winter of 1926, the South City, due to the aftermath of the war, the local vitality had not yet recovered, the district gentry approved to temporarily collect taxes at 75% of the fixed rate, so they still follow the old method. However, this is a temporary expedient measure, and there is no reason to remain unchanged. Therefore, it has been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval, starting this spring, the 75% discount will be canceled to comply with the tax regulations, and return to uniformity. It is estimated that annual revenue can be increased by more than 300,000 yuan. In addition, the wharf tax was collected by the Shanghai Customs, with an annual income of approximately 800,000 taels. Among them, the merchant ship tax from the South City and Pudong wharves is about 400,000 taels, but in fact, the Jianghai Customs only allocates 10,000 yuan to the Municipal Government each year. Last year, the Municipal Government negotiated with the concession authorities, arguing that the distribution of wharf taxes was unfair, and agreed to change the collection of the Pudong and South City areas to the Municipal Government based on the location and area of cargo handling. This case has now been finalized, and it is estimated that annual revenue will increase by more than 600,000 yuan.

▲ Planning Business Tax: The business tax is a source of municipal revenue according to the Municipal Organization Law. This city prepared for the business tax before the two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, but due to the complexity of the situation, it did not hesitate to extensively consult opinions and study in detail, so the announcement was later. The proposed plan for the city's central area cannot be easily implemented without actual financial resources, and the business tax is one way to promote the success of construction projects. However, this city is determined to adopt several principles in collecting business tax: (1) do not disturb the people, (2) adopt the opinions of local people, and (3) the tax rate should be the rate recognized by the central government, not higher than those of various provinces. Currently, the collection regulations and travel plan draft have been drafted, and the tax rate layer is particularly complicated, so we must be careful in doing things. We are now studying it in detail and it will be announced soon.

▲ Raising Municipal Bonds: This city issued 3 million yuan of municipal bonds in 1929, originally intended for 1.2 million yuan for the first phase of the construction of the city's main roads, 500,000 yuan for part of the construction of the city's central area, 210,000 yuan for the reorganization of old bonds, and 1 million yuan for opening a municipal bank. At that time, the Municipal Bond Solicitation Committee was established and divided into solicitation. The collected funds, estimated at 1 million yuan, were first allocated to the municipal bank fund, so the municipal bank opened in February of the 19th year. The old bonds of the former municipal agencies were prepared for reorganization and submitted to the municipal government for approval, and then posted in the newspaper to announce the exchange of municipal bond tickets by the municipal bank to comfort the citizens' eagerness. Later, due to military influence, the bond solicitation was only one-third. Until October of last year, the Municipal Bond Solicitation Committee drafted three measures and submitted them to the Construction Discussion Committee for resolution: (1) Collect payments separately from households that have recognized but not paid, (2) Borrow and collect rent to exchange for municipal bonds, which is to use the balance of the previously determined total amount of two months' rent collection after deducting 1 million yuan for short-term treasury bills for the 19th year's customs duties, and (3) All industries in this city will be apportioned at the same time. After submitting it to the Municipal Government for announcement and implementation, the borrowing and collection of rent has now come to an end. It is estimated that 1.5 to 1.6 million yuan of municipal bonds will be sold, which will be used exclusively for prescribed projects, so that construction can be completed early.

▲ Recovering the South Wharf: The South City coastline wharf and the along-Pu public land are interrelated and urgently need to be reorganized. The former Port Authority was ordered to organize an evaluation committee to evaluate the prices of the wharves owned by Dada, Datong, and Minxing companies, as well as their attached buildings, and recover them for municipal operation. It was submitted to the Municipal Government for approval, and the former Port Authority was convened to take over the wharves of the companies separately. On the one hand, the value of the wharf assets to be paid to the companies, as well as subsidies and repayment of loans, totaled more than 780,000 yuan, which were raised clearly. After the wharf is recovered, the annual income from rent and berthing fees, etc., is estimated to be more than 200,000 yuan.

Establishment of Municipal Treasury: This city's finances, in terms of disbursement, have been handled by the fourth section of the Municipal Government Finance Bureau. Now, in order to separate accounting and disbursement, a municipal treasury is being established. It is expected to be officially established around July of this year, with a treasurer responsible for handling its affairs. Regarding the payment of funds, it is carried out under the order of the Finance Bureau.

Xu Shiying, Wang Yiting, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Shi Liangcai, Huang Hanzhi, Zhang Gongquan, Wang Binchan, Wang Yansong, Wu Nanhao, Xie Hengchuan, Zhang Zilian, Sun Longji, and other gentlemen hosted a banquet at the Jue Lin Vegetarian Restaurant last night at 6:00 PM to welcome philanthropist Mr. Zhu Ziqiao. ▲ Brief Announcement: The disaster situation in Shaanxi is extremely serious, unprecedented. Mr. Zhu Ziqiao, with a charitable heart, raised huge sums of money and went to provide relief himself. He has traveled to and from Shaanxi three times since last year, with perseverance, admired by the world. However, the floods are still severe, and the spring plowing season is approaching, so relief is particularly urgent. Therefore, Mr. Zhu Ziqiao resolutely came to Shanghai to appeal for the 8 million disaster victims in Shaanxi. We and others live in peace and happiness, and we are saddened by the suffering of our compatriots in Shaanxi. Thinking of this, we are heartbroken. We hereby issue a brief announcement, urgently appealing to all charitable people, ladies and sisters at home and abroad to show compassion, donate money to provide relief, and the merits and rewards will be boundless. We are extremely grateful.

▲ Articles of Association: (1) All attendees today are members of the fundraising committee of this association. (2) The initiating members shall elect 80 executive committee members and 5 supervisory committee members. (3) The executive committee members shall elect 19 standing committee members. (4) The standing committee members shall elect 7 presidium members. (5) This association shall have four groups: A. General Affairs Group, responsible for documents, accounting, general affairs, register creation, and matters not belonging to other groups. B. Finance Group, responsible for receiving accounts, depositing, remitting, and purchasing grain. C. Relief Group, responsible for investigation, distribution, and work relief matters. D. Publicity Group, responsible for compiling disaster situation reports, publishing advertisements, and fundraising matters. (6) The General Affairs, Finance, Relief, and Publicity groups shall be elected by the executive committee members, with two or three members serving in each group. (7) The standing committee shall hire several staff members to be responsible for the affairs of each group. (8) All of the above members are volunteer positions. (9) For writing documents, donation books, etc., employees may be hired and given allowances. (10) Locations for collecting donations: China Jiseihui, Relief Committee Office. (11) The fundraising period is limited to one month from the date of establishment of this association. (12) This organization's articles of association shall be implemented from the date of resolution by the entire committee.

Chiang Ti-hsien's Discussion on Cotton Production

▲ Attention from the Cotton Industry

The Chinese Cotton Production Improvement and Statistics Conference, initiated by the Chinese Cotton Mill Owners' Association and the provincial cotton fields of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shandong, Hunan, Shanxi, and Shaanxi provinces, the provincial agricultural fields of Jiangxi and Anhui provinces, the Hubei Cotton Industry Improvement Committee, the Agricultural Extension Department of Henan University, and the Zhengding Cotton Field of the Ministry of Industry, has been actively preparing and is scheduled to open at 2:00 PM on March 15th. Reporters from various newspapers inquired about the purpose of the conference to Mr. Chiang Ti-hsien, who is in charge of the conference preparation. He briefly stated that since the end of the European War, the domestic cotton textile industry has developed rapidly. In the past decade, the number of spindles has increased from two million to four million. Each spindle uses 200 catties of cotton per year, requiring a total of 8 million piculs. According to recent surveys by the Cotton Mill Owners' Association, the national cotton production in recent years has averaged no more than 7 million piculs, which is already insufficient to meet demand. This does not even include the cotton needed for clothing and bedding. Living standards in the interior are relatively low, and cotton consumption for clothing and bedding is at its highest, also accounting for 2 to 3 million piculs nationwide. Domestic supply is insufficient, making it necessary to import from foreign countries. As a result, imports of American and Indian cotton have increased significantly. Recent imports of foreign cotton totaled 2.41 million piculs in the sixteenth year, 1.91 million piculs in the seventeenth year, 2.51 million piculs in the eighteenth year, and 2.71 million piculs in the nineteenth year. Cotton exports, on the other hand, decreased from 1.44 million piculs in the sixteenth year to 230,000 piculs in the nineteenth year. The value of cotton imports in the nineteenth year exceeded 100 million taels, already ranking third among imported goods. The largest drain on our country's trade has always been the 200 million taels for cotton goods. Now, cotton alone exceeds 100 million taels, which is probably unknown to most people. In recent years, American and Indian cotton prices have been low, making purchases not very difficult. However, can it be guaranteed that prices will remain low? Therefore, the suffering felt by the textile industry regarding raw materials and the cotton drain will undoubtedly increase with time. Furthermore, with social progress, cotton products are becoming increasingly refined. Domestic cotton has short and coarse fibers, making it unsuitable for fine spinning, leading to a significant increase in American cotton imports. Therefore, improving and promoting our country's cotton production is a matter of utmost urgency. Our country has vast regions suitable for cotton cultivation. Jiangsu is known for its small land area and dense population, but according to reliable surveys, there are still over 20 million mu of land that can be reclaimed for cotton planting. The situation in other provinces is likely similar. If we can work hard to promote this, we can not only achieve self-sufficiency but also meet the needs of other countries. It would not be difficult to seize the authority over world cotton production currently held by the United States. Recently, the British economic mission came to China and repeatedly inquired about the state of China's cotton production, especially paying attention to the achievements in improvement. We felt unable to answer. Currently, most cotton-producing provinces in the country have established provincial cotton fields to oversee cotton production improvement work throughout the province. However, they operate independently and lack coordination. The primary purpose of this conference is to connect the organizations in various provinces that are practically engaged in cotton planting, so that they can exchange reports and recognize each other regarding the national cotton production situation, and jointly discuss comprehensive methods for improving and promoting cotton production nationwide. Secondly, the four countries with the highest cotton production in the world are the United States, India, China, and Egypt. Except for our country, governments in these countries have specially established bureaus for cotton production, spending vast sums of money on statistics. In our country, the Cotton Mill Owners' Association has been responsible for this work since 1919, but its efforts have been insufficient. Therefore, there has been little progress in the past twelve years. In recent years, with the support of cotton industry organizations in various provinces, we have been striving to improve the methods, but the conditions in each province are different. It is necessary to agree on methods suitable for the entire country, and revising the estimations is especially urgent. Accurate predictions of cotton harvests allow the domestic and foreign cotton industries to be aware of the supply situation early and adjust accordingly. For example, the recent sharp rise in cotton prices on the exchange, which led to a market shutdown, was largely due to the fact that most people were unaware of the poor harvest of Chinese cotton last year and sold excessively. In the future, as the domestic cotton industry develops further, these estimates will become increasingly important, so that we can eliminate the danger of significant gaps between supply and demand occurring without early remedial action. Furthermore, investigation and improvement are closely related. We must first understand the cotton production situation in various places before we can talk about improvement. We must first understand the progress and decline of cotton production in a certain place before we know the urgency of promotion. In recent years, Japanese cotton merchants in China have been sending personnel to cotton-producing areas during the cotton harvesting season to conduct investigations and publish forecast reports. The cotton industry treasures these reports like precious jade. Chinese cotton production, Chinese people cannot conduct their own investigations, and rely solely on the Japanese. This is truly regrettable. Therefore, this conference brings together cotton fields from various provinces to jointly discuss national cotton production estimation plans, divide the work, and cooperate to achieve effective results. There have been many conferences in the country in recent years, but few have been as narrowly focused as cotton production improvement and cotton production statistics. In fact, basic construction should start with simple tasks. This conference focuses on discussion, and motions must be approved by all representatives from the provinces before they are passed, so that they can be implemented. Recently, some conferences have resolved hundreds of motions in a single day, but we dare not hope for such results. If we can only complete one motion in seven days and the representatives bring it back to implement it, that is what we desire. Furthermore, since this news was announced, many have written to request to join. Invitation cards have already been distributed to the domestic cotton industry, but omissions are inevitable. The purpose of the conference is to improve Chinese cotton production and conduct estimations, relying on the joint efforts of the entire country. We sincerely welcome all sectors to participate and discuss everything, regardless of whether they initiated the conference or not.
